## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / kinetic ODE modeling)
**Analysis**: The target is dA_dt, explicitly the time-derivative of a concentration A(t), which is the standard representation of chemical kinetics via rate laws and ordinary differential equations. With only t and A available, the most likely structures are phenomenological rate laws (zero/first/second/nth order), equilibrium-relaxation forms, autocatalysis, and time-varying effective rate coefficients due to changing conditions.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (surface-limited or catalyst-saturated regime where rate is independent of A)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive/thermal decomposition, pseudo-first-order kinetics)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or second-order in a single reactant approximation)
- Nth-order power-law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical overall reaction order or complex mechanism lumping)
- Production with first-order loss: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (continuous feed/formation plus linear consumption)
- Relaxation to equilibrium (linear): dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (approach to a steady-state/equilibrium concentration c1)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-type kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating growth with depletion/limitation)
- Inhibited-order (effective rate decreases at high A): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (self-inhibition or crowding/transport limitation captured by a rational rate law)
- Mixed-order / parallel paths: dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (simultaneous first- and second-order loss channels)
- Time-varying first-order rate (linear ramp): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (changing conditions such as temperature ramp or catalyst deactivation/activation approximated in time)
- Time-varying first-order rate (exponential drift): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (accelerating/decaying effective rate coefficient over time)
- Forced kinetics (periodic or programmed input): dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (external forcing or periodic modulation of conditions approximated directly in time)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is strictly negative and scales linearly with A over the dataset, a first-order decay form (-c*A) is strongly indicated.
- If dA_dt remains near a constant negative value while A varies widely, that suggests a zero-order regime (rate-limited by catalyst/site saturation or mass transfer).
- If dA_dt vs A is strongly curved and becomes much more negative at higher A, quadratic or general power-law dependence (-c*A**n, n>1) is typical of bimolecular/overall higher-order behavior.
- If dA_dt crosses zero at a positive A and changes sign around that point, an equilibrium-relaxation form c*(A_eq - A) (or nonlinear variants) is suggested.
- If dA_dt is near zero when A is near zero (but negative for A>0), consumption laws proportional to A (or A**n) are more physical than a pure constant term.
- If the magnitude of dA_dt decreases at high A (sublinear growth in |dA_dt|), rational inhibition-like forms such as -c*A/(1+c*A) can capture saturation/inhibition/transport limitations.
- If residuals show systematic drift with time even at similar A values, incorporate explicit t-dependence via a time-varying effective rate coefficient (e.g., (c0+c1*t)*A or exp(c*t)*A).
- If dA_dt is positive at low A but becomes negative at high A (or vice versa), autocatalytic/limited-growth structures like c*A*(c1-A) can model self-acceleration with depletion/limitation.

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK23)
============================================================
GT: -c0*sqrt(A) + c1*_p*sin(c2*A)
Candidate formulas: 77

GT is the fixed function (independent of \(t\)):
\[
f(A)= -0.1001695596\,\sqrt{A} + 0.4714850169\,\sin(0.8555148186\,A).
\]
So any matching candidate must be able (by choosing its own constants) to produce **exactly** “(constant)\(\cdot\sqrt{A}\) + (constant)\(\cdot\sin(\text{constant}\cdot A)\)” with **no extra dependence** (no constant offset, no cos term, no logs/exp/rational-in-\(A\), no \(t\)).

Below, for each candidate, I check whether all non-GT structures can be eliminated by setting parameters to 0 (or otherwise), and whether the remaining structure can be tuned to the GT.

---

### 1.
Has rational factors \((A+c1)^{-1}\) and extra \(\sin(\log(\cdot))\). Cannot become \(\sqrt{A}+\sin(kA)\) for all \(A\). **No**.

### 2.
Contains \(t\)-dependent \(c7*exp(c8*t)*log(\cdot)\) unless forced to 0; also has log term and constant offset. Even if set log and offset to 0, left with only a sine (no \(\sqrt{A}\) term). **No**.

### 3.
Has \(\sqrt{A}c0\) but also constant \(c1\), cosine, and \(exp(c6*cos(\cdot))\). You can zero out extra terms, leaving \(\sqrt{A}c0\) only (no sine). **No**.

### 4.
Sine + constant + logs. Can zero logs and constant, leaving sine only (no \(\sqrt{A}\)). **No**.

### 5.
\(\sqrt{A}c0\) plus cosine terms; can remove extras but then no sine. **No**.

### 6.
Polynomial + sine + constant + log. Can remove polynomial/log/constant, leaving sine only. No \(\sqrt{A}\). **No**.

### 7.
Rational \(A c0/(A c1+1)\) and cosine term etc. Even if remove extras, cannot create \(\sqrt{A}\) term. **No**.

### 8.
\(\sqrt{A}c0\) plus cosine and \(exp(Ac6)\cos(\cdot)\). Can remove extras, leaving only \(\sqrt{A}\). No sine. **No**.

### 9.
Has \(A^2\), \(A^{c1}\log(\cdot)\), sine, constant. You can keep sine and kill others, but no \(\sqrt{A}\). **No**.

### 10.
\(\sqrt{A}c0\) plus rational-in-\(A^{c1}\) and cosine and constant. Can kill extra terms, leaving \(\sqrt{A}\) only. No sine. **No**.

### 11.
\[
\sqrt{A}\,c0 + c1\sin(Ac2+c3)
\]
This has exactly the needed functional forms. Choose:
- \(c0=-0.10016955960092372\)
- \(c1=0.47148501687516587\)
- \(c2=0.8555148185506902\)
- \(c3=0\) (or \(2\pi n\))
Then candidate 11 equals GT for all \(A\). **Yes**.

### 12.
Sine + constant + \(\log(\cdot)/\sqrt{A}\). Cannot produce \(\sqrt{A}\) term. **No**.

### 13.
Sine + constant + \(\sqrt{|A|}\). GT uses \(\sqrt{A}\) (not \(\sqrt{|A|}\)); unless domain is restricted to \(A\ge 0\) (not stated), not equivalent as functions of real \(A\). Also has constant offset. Even if constant set to 0, still \(\sqrt{|A|}\neq \sqrt{A}\) for negative \(A\). **No**.

### 14.
\(\sqrt{A}c0 + c1 + c2\cos(\cdot)\). Can’t make a sine term without leaving cosine (cos cannot equal sin(kA) for all A unless amplitude 0). **No**.

### 15.
Has \(A^{c0}c1\) plus sine plus constant. You could set \(A^{c0}\) to \(\sqrt{A}\) by \(c0=1/2\), but then it’s \(c1\sqrt{A}\) **plus** sine **plus** constant; constant can be 0, so structure could match GT if sine is \(\sin(kA)\) with no phase? Actually it has \(c2\sin(Ac3+c4)\) which is fine. So candidate 15 can match too by:
- \(c0=1/2,\ c1=-0.1001695596\)
- \(c2=0.4714850169,\ c3=0.8555148186,\ c4=0\)
- \(c5=0\)
Thus **Yes** (also matches).

### 16.
\(\sqrt{A}c0 + c1\sin(Ac2+c3)+c4\). Set \(c4=0\) and tune others as in #11. **Yes**.

### 17.
Contains linear/power terms plus sine plus cosine plus constant. You can set unwanted coefficients to 0, leaving sine only (no \(\sqrt{A}\)). **No**.

### 18.
Power terms plus sine plus constant. No \(\sqrt{A}\) unless you use \(A^{c1}c2\) as \(\sqrt{A}\) by \(c1=1/2\). Then you’d have \(\sqrt{A}c2 + c3\sin(\cdot)+c6\). Set \(c6=0\) and tune. This matches GT. **Yes**.

### 19.
\(\sqrt{A}c0 + A^2c1 + c2 + c3\cos(\cdot)\). Can remove \(A^2\), constant, cosine, leaving only \(\sqrt{A}\). No sine. **No**.

### 20.
Same issue as 19 plus linear term. No sine. **No**.

### 21.
\(A^{c0}c1\sin(\cdot)+A^{c4}c5+c6\). Hard to get “\(\sqrt{A}\) + \sin(kA)\)” as a sum: sine is multiplied by a power of \(A\). To match GT, that power must be \(A^0\) so \(c0=0\), giving constant-amplitude sine; then remaining \(A^{c4}c5\) must be \(\sqrt{A}\) so \(c4=1/2\). Then it can match with \(c6=0\). **Yes**.

### 22.
Has \(A^2\) plus \(A^{c1}\sin(\cdot)\) plus another sine plus constant. To match GT, need one sine term with constant amplitude and one \(\sqrt{A}\) term; but there is no standalone \(\sqrt{A}\) term. If you try to use \(A^{c1}\sin(\cdot)\) with \(c1=1/2\), you get \(\sqrt{A}\sin(kA)\), not allowed. **No**.

### 23.
All terms are rational with denominator \(A+c1\). Cannot equal \(\sqrt{A}\) and \(\sin(kA)\) globally. **No**.

### 24.
Linear term + \(A^{c1}\log\) + sine + constant. No \(\sqrt{A}\) unless via log term (impossible). **No**.

### 25.
Rational terms plus \(A^{c5}c6\). Denominator prevents matching \(\sqrt{A}\) and sine without rational distortion. **No**.

### 26.
\(\sqrt{A}c0\) plus rational \(A c1/(A+c2)\) plus constant plus cosine. No sine. **No**.

### 27.
\(\sqrt{A}c0 + A^{c1}c2 + c3 + c4\cos(\cdot)\). No sine. **No**.

### 28.
Has \(t\)-dependent \(A^{c1}c2\exp(c3 t)\) unless killed; remaining has cosine not sine. **No**.

### 29.
Rational + power + sine + constant. No \(\sqrt{A}\) unless power term is \(\sqrt{A}\) (set \(c2=1/2\)), but then still have rational term which must be 0 (set \(c0=0\)). Then it becomes \(\sqrt{A}c3 + c4\sin(\cdot)+c7\). Set \(c7=0\) and tune sine. **Yes**.

### 30.
\(A c0 + A^{c1}c2 + c3\sin(\cdot)+c6\). Set \(c0=0\), choose \(c1=1/2\) to get \(\sqrt{A}\), set \(c6=0\), tune sine. **Yes**.

### 31.
\(\sqrt{A}c0 + A c1 + c2 + c3\cos(\cdot)\). No sine. **No**.

### 32.
Has \(t\)-dependent power term unless killed; also sine multiplied by \(A^{c0}\). Could set \(c0=0\) to make sine amplitude constant and kill the \(t\)-dependent term by setting \(c5=0\). Then only sine + constant remains (no \(\sqrt{A}\)). **No**.

### 33.
Power term + sine + constant + log. Can set log and constant 0, set power to \(\sqrt{A}\) via \(c0=1/2\). Then matches. **Yes**.

### 34.
\(\sqrt{A}c0\) plus rational plus constant plus cosine. No sine. **No**.

### 35.
Has \(t\)-dependent log term unless killed; remaining cosine not sine. **No**.

### 36.
Has many extra structures; only sine present but no \(\sqrt{A}\) term. **No**.

### 37–38.
Cosine + log terms; no sine. **No** for both.

### 39.
Has \(t\) explicitly and cosine; no sine. **No**.

### 40.
Has \(t\)-dependent log unless killed; remaining is rational + sine + constant. No \(\sqrt{A}\). **No**.

### 41–42.
Contain polynomials/logs/cos/sin; no \(\sqrt{A}\) term. **No**.

### 43.
Sine multiplied by \(A^{c0}\) and plus \(A^{c4}\log(\cdot)\). Hard to get pure \(\sqrt{A}\) plus pure sine: if \(c0=0\) gives constant-amplitude sine, but \(\sqrt{A}\) cannot be made from \(A^{c4}\log(\cdot)\) for all \(A\). **No**.

### 44–48.
Various polynomial/log/cos structures; none can yield exactly \(\sqrt{A}\) plus sine without extra terms. **No**.

### 49–51.
Rational-in-\(A\) plus other terms; cannot match GT’s non-rational \(\sqrt{A}\) term. **No**.

### 52.
Has cosine and \(t\)-dependent cosine product; no sine. **No**.

### 53–60.
Contain exp/log/cos/powers but not the exact additive \(\sqrt{A}\) + sine structure without extra nonremovable forms (or sine is inside exp). **No**.

### 61–77.
All remaining either lack \(\sqrt{A}\) as an additive term, or include unavoidable rational/log/exp/\(t\) dependence, or have sine multiplied by powers/logs. None can be reduced to exactly \(-0.1001695\sqrt{A}+0.4714850\sin(0.8555148A)\) for all \(A\). **No**.
